-4.71,1.57 -4.83,0.99 -4.95,0.40 -4.93,-0.19 -4.91,-0.79 -4.74,-1.36 -4.57,-1.94 -4.27,-2.46 -3.97,-2.98 -3.56,-3.41 -3.14,-3.85 -3.14,-3.84 L -3.14,-3.84 Z"></path></g></svg>
$U_{2}=0V$
$K(0)=\frac{0V}{U_{1}}=0$

$K(j\omega)=\frac{U_{2}(j\omega)}{U_{1}(j\omega)}$
$K(j\omega)=\underbrace{ K(\omega) }_{ ch. ampl. }e^{j \underbrace{ \varphi(\omega) }_{ ch. f }}$
$K(\omega)=|\frac{U_{2}(j\omega)}{U_{1}(j\omega)}|=\frac{|U_{2}(j\omega)|}{|U_{1}(j\omega)|}=\frac{U_{2RMS}}{U_{1RMS}}$

case 2
$f\to \infty(\omega\to infty)$

case 3
$\omega_{0}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{ LC }}$
$f_{0}=\frac{\omega_{0}}{2\pi}=\frac{1}{2\pi \sqrt{ LC }}$

example data
$L=200mH$
$C=20µF$
$R_{L}=9kΩ$
$K(f_{0})=\frac{U_{2RMS}}{U_{1RMS}}$=$\frac{\cancel{ U_{1RMS} }·\frac{R_{L}}{R+R_{L}}}{\cancel{ U_{1RMS }}}$=$\frac{R_{L}}{R+R_{L}}=\frac{9kΩ}{12kΩ}=\frac{3}{4}$

$f_{0}=\frac{1}{6.28\sqrt{ 4000·10^{-9} }}=80Hz$

---

# Ex.2

Find the gain of the given bands stop filter at the center frequency BSF (FPZ)
$K(\omega)=\frac{U_{2}(\omega)}{U_{1}(\omega)}$

$L=10mH$
$C=10µF$

$U_{2}=U_{1}· \frac{R_{L}}{R+R_{L}}$
$K(0))=\frac{R_{L}}{R+R_{L}}$

if $\omega=\omega_{0}$ LC -> short
$K(\omega_{0})=0V$

# 3
Calculate overvolt gain in decibels of this cascaded amplifier

$L_{TOT}=?[dB]$
$k_{1}=9\left[ \frac{v}{v} \right]$
$k_{2}=2\left[ \frac{v}{v} \right]$

font-family="Nunito, sans-serif, Segoe UI Emoji" font-size="28px" fill="#1e1e1e" text-anchor="start" style="white-space: pre;" direction="ltr" dominant-baseline="alphabetic">U in</text></g><g transform="translate(330 170) rotate(0 18.634071350097656 17.5)"><text x="0" y="26.712" font-family="Nunito, sans-serif, Segoe UI Emoji" font-size="28px" fill="#1e1e1e" text-anchor="start" style="white-space: pre;" direction="ltr" dominant-baseline="alphabetic">U3</text></g><g transform="translate(670 170) rotate(0 34.650146484375 17.5)"><text x="0" y="26.712" font-family="Nunito, sans-serif, Segoe UI Emoji" font-size="28px" fill="#1e1e1e" text-anchor="start" style="white-space: pre;" direction="ltr" dominant-baseline="alphabetic">U out</text></g></svg>
$U_{3}=U_{IN}·k_{1}$
$U_{OUT}=U_{3}·k_{2}$
$U_{OUT}=U_{IN}·k_{1}·k_{2}$

$K_{TOT}=\frac{U_{OUT}}{U_{IN}}=k_{1}·k_{2}=9·2=18\left[ \frac{v}{v} \right]$

$\boxed{L[dB]=20\log_{10}(K)}$
total:
$L_{TOT}=20\log_{10}(18)=25.1dB$

individual
$L_{TOT}=20\log(K)=20\log(k_{1}·k_{2})=\underbrace{ 20\log(k_{1}) }_{ L_{1} }+\underbrace{ 20\log k_{2} }_{ L_{2} }$
$L_{1}=20\log 9=19.08dB$
$L_{2}=20\log 2=6.02dB$

---

# 4

calculate at the cutoff frequency  (border frequency)

usually defined 3dB under max

minumum allowed frequency for filter is 60dB
60dB or greater is good enough

$L(\omega c)=L_{max}-3dB$ ->  $K(\omega c)=\frac{K_{MAX}}{\sqrt{ 2 }}=\frac{0.4}{\sqrt{ 2 }}$

$L=20\log K$
$L(\omega c)=L_{MAX}-3dB$
$20\log K(\omega c)=20\log K_{MAX}-\underbrace{ 3dB }_{ 20\log x }$
$20\log x=-3db$
$x=10^{-3/20}=0.707=\frac{1}{\sqrt{ 2 }}$

$K(\omega c)=\frac{K_{MAX}}{\sqrt{ 2 }}=\frac{0.4}{\sqrt{ 2 }}$

japan makes 1dB headphones very good

# 5
for the assumed 6kH cutoff frequency calculate size noise filtering capacitor

font-family="Nunito, sans-serif, Segoe UI Emoji" font-size="20px" fill="#1e1e1e" text-anchor="start" style="white-space: pre;" direction="ltr" dominant-baseline="alphabetic">R1=14kΩ</text></g></svg>
$K(j\omega)=\frac{U_{2}(j\omega)}{U_{1}(j\omega)}$

Z- capacitor || $R_{2}$

$U_{2}=\frac{Z(j\omega)}{R_{1}+Z(j\omega)}$

$Z(j\omega)=\frac{Z_{C}·R_{2}}{Z_{C}+R_{2}}= \frac{\frac{1}{j\omega c}·R_{2}}{-j \frac{1}{\omega c}+R_{2}}=\frac{R_{2}}{1+j\omega R_{2}C}$

$K(j\omega)=\frac{Z}{R_{1}+Z}=\frac{\frac{R_{2}}{1+j\omega R_{2}C}}{R_{1}+\frac{R_{2}}{1+j\omega R_{2}C}}=\frac{R_{2}}{R_{1}+j\omega R_{1}R_{2}C+R_{2}}=\frac{R_{2}}{R_{1}+R_{2}+j\omega R_{1}R_{2}C}$
$K(\omega)=|K(j\omega)|=\frac{R_{2}}{\sqrt{ (R_{1}+R_{2})^{2}+(\omega R_{1}R_{2}C)^{2} }}$
$\frac{R_{2}}{R_{1}+R_{2}}=\frac{16kΩ}{30kΩ}=0.53$

0.59,-0.54 0.65,-0.47 0.65,-0.47 L 0.65,-0.47 Z"></path></g></svg>
$\omega_{C}=2\pi F_{C}$

$K(\omega c)=\frac{K_{MAX}}{\sqrt{ 2 }}=\frac{\frac{R_{2}}{R_{1}+R_{2}}}{\sqrt{ 2 }}$=$\frac{R_{2}}{\sqrt{ (R_{1}+R_{2})^{2}+(\omega R_{1}R_{2}C)^{2} }}=$ 

$=\frac{1}{(R_{1}+R_{2})\sqrt{ 2 }}\to \sqrt{ (R_{1}+R_{2})^{2}+(\omega_{C}R_{1}R_{2}C) }=(R_{1}+R_{2})\sqrt{ 2 }$
$(\omega _{C}R_{1}R_{2}C)^{2}=(R_{1}+R_{2})^{2}$
$\omega_{C}R_{1}R_{2}C=R_{1}+R_{2}$

$C=\frac{R_{1}+R_{2}}{\omega_{C}R_{1}R_{2}}=\frac{R_{1}+R_{2}}{2\pi f_{C}·R_{1}R_{2}}=\frac{30kΩ}{6.28·6khz·14kΩ·16kΩ}=\frac{30}{6.28·6·14M}$
$=\frac{30µF}{6.28·6·14}=3.56nF$

---

sketch the DC gain in log form

$R_{1}=R_{2}=R$
$K(\omega)=\frac{R_{2}}{\sqrt{ (R_{1}+R_{2})^{2}+(\omega R_{1}R_{2}C)^{2} }}=\frac{\cancel{ R }}{\sqrt{ (2\cancel{ R })^{2}+(\omega R^{\cancel{ 2 }}C)^{2} }}$=
=$\frac{1}{\sqrt{ 4+(\omega RC)^{2} }}$

$L(\omega)20\log\left( \frac{1}{\sqrt{ 4+(\omega RC)^{2} }} \right)=$
			$(4+(\omega RC)^{2})^{-1/2}$		

Bodhi aproximation

$L(\omega)=-10\log[4+(\omega RC)^{2}]$

1. $\omega$ small
$\omega RC<4$
$\frac{\omega RC}{4}<1$
$\frac{(\omega RC)^{2}}{4}\ll 1$
$\omega< \frac{4}{RC}\to 4+(\omega RC)^{2}\equiv4\to$
$L(\omega)-10\log4=-6dB=const$

2. $\omega> \frac{4}{RC}$
$\frac{\omega RC}{4}>1$
 $\frac{(\omega RC)^{2}}{4}\gg1\to 4+(\omega RC)^{2}\equiv(\omega RC)^{2}$
 $L(\omega)=-10\log[(\omega RC)^{2}]=-20\log(\omega RC)$
